   <h1 id="firstHeading" class="firstHeading">Grenada</h1> 
   <div id="bodyContent" class="vector-body"> 
    <div id="siteSub" class="noprint">
     From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia
    </div> 
    <div id="contentSub"></div> 
    <div id="contentSub2"></div>

     <div class="mw-parser-output">
      <div class="shortdescription nomobile noexcerpt noprint searchaux" style="display:none">
       Country in the West Indies in the Caribbean Sea
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       This article is about the island country in the Caribbean. For other usage, see <a href="/wiki/Grenada_(disambiguation)" class="mw-disambig" title="Grenada (disambiguation)">Grenada (disambiguation)</a>.
      </div>

      <p><b>Grenada</b> (<span class="rt-commentedText nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ɡ/: 'g' in 'guy'">ɡ</span><span title="'r' in 'rye'">r</span><span title="/ə/: 'a' in 'about'">ə</span><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="'n' in 'nigh'">n</span><span title="/eɪ/: 'a' in 'face'">eɪ</span><span title="'d' in 'dye'">d</span><span title="/ə/: 'a' in 'about'">ə</span></span>/</a></span> <span class="nowrap" style="font-size:85%">(<span class="unicode haudio"><span class="fn"><span style="white-space:nowrap;margin-right:.25em;"><a href="/wiki/File:En-us-Grenada.ogg" title="About this sound"><img alt="About this sound" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" decoding="async" width="11" height="11" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="20" data-file-height="20"></a></span><a href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/c/c0/En-us-Grenada.ogg" class="internal" title="En-us-Grenada.ogg">listen</a></span></span>)</span></span> <a href="/wiki/Help:Pronunciation_respelling_key" title="Help:Pronunciation respelling key"><i title="English pronunciation respelling">grə-<span style="font-size:90%">NAY</span>-də</i></a>; <a href="/wiki/Grenadian_Creole_French" title="Grenadian Creole French">Grenadian Creole French</a>: <i>Gwenad</i>) is an island country in the <a href="/wiki/West_Indies" title="West Indies">West Indies</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Caribbean_Sea" title="Caribbean Sea">Caribbean Sea</a> at the southern end of the <a href="/wiki/Grenadines" title="Grenadines">Grenadines</a> island chain. Grenada consists of the island of Grenada itself, two smaller islands, <a href="/wiki/Carriacou" title="Carriacou">Carriacou</a> and <a href="/wiki/Petite_Martinique" title="Petite Martinique">Petite Martinique</a>, and several small islands which lie to the north of the main island and are a part of <a href="/wiki/The_Grenadines" class="mw-redirect" title="The Grenadines">the Grenadines</a>. It is located northwest of <a href="/wiki/Trinidad_and_Tobago" title="Trinidad and Tobago">Trinidad and Tobago</a>, northeast of <a href="/wiki/Venezuela" title="Venezuela">Venezuela</a> and southwest of <a href="/wiki/Saint_Vincent_and_the_Grenadines" title="Saint Vincent and the Grenadines">Saint Vincent and the Grenadines</a>. Its size is 348.5 square kilometres (134.6&nbsp;sq&nbsp;mi), and it had an estimated population of 112,523 in July 2020.<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_World_Factbook_-_Grenada_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA_World_Factbook_-_Grenada-8">[8]</a></sup> Its capital is <a href="/wiki/St._George%27s,_Grenada" title="St. George's, Grenada">St. George's</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_World_Factbook_-_Grenada_8-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA_World_Factbook_-_Grenada-8">[8]</a></sup> Grenada is also known as the "Island of Spice" due to its production of <a href="/wiki/Nutmeg" title="Nutmeg">nutmeg</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mace_(spice)" class="mw-redirect" title="Mace (spice)">mace</a> crops.<sup id="cite_ref-britannica.com_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-britannica.com-9">[9]</a></sup> </p>
      <p><span style="font-size: small;"><span id="coordinates"><a href="/wiki/Geographic_coordinate_system" title="Geographic coordinate system">Coordinates</a>: 
         <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r994658806"><span class="plainlinks nourlexpansion"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="//geohack.toolforge.org/geohack.php?pagename=Grenada&amp;params=12_07_N_61_40_W_"><span class="geo-default"><span class="geo-dms" title="Maps, aerial photos, and other data for this location"><span class="latitude">12°07′N</span> <span class="longitude">61°40′W</span></span></span><span class="geo-multi-punct">﻿ / ﻿</span><span class="geo-nondefault"><span class="geo-dec" title="Maps, aerial photos, and other data for this location">12.117°N 61.667°W</span><span style="display:none">﻿ / <span class="geo">12.117; -61.667</span></span></span></a></span></span></span> Before the <a href="/wiki/European_colonization_of_the_Americas" title="European colonization of the Americas">arrival of Europeans in the Americas</a>, Grenada was inhabited by the <a href="/wiki/Indigenous_peoples_of_the_Americas" title="Indigenous peoples of the Americas">indigenous</a> <a href="/wiki/Arawaks" class="mw-redirect" title="Arawaks">Arawaks</a> and later by the <a href="/wiki/Island_Caribs" class="mw-redirect" title="Island Caribs">Island Caribs</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_World_Factbook_-_Grenada_8-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA_World_Factbook_-_Grenada-8">[8]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Christopher_Columbus" title="Christopher Columbus">Christopher Columbus</a> sighted Grenada in 1498 during his <a href="/wiki/Voyages_of_Christopher_Columbus" title="Voyages of Christopher Columbus">third voyage</a> to the Americas.<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_World_Factbook_-_Grenada_8-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA_World_Factbook_-_Grenada-8">[8]</a></sup> Following several unsuccessful attempts by Europeans to colonise the island due to resistance from the Island Caribs, <a href="/wiki/French_colonial_empire" title="French colonial empire">French</a> settlement and colonisation began in 1650 and continued for the next century. On 10 February 1763, Grenada was ceded to the <a href="/wiki/British_Empire" title="British Empire">British</a> under the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Paris_(1763)" title="Treaty of Paris (1763)">Treaty of Paris</a>. British rule continued until 1974 (except for a <a href="/wiki/Capture_of_Grenada_(1779)" title="Capture of Grenada (1779)">period of French rule</a> between 1779 and 1783). From 1958 to 1962 Grenada was part of the <a href="/wiki/Federation_of_the_West_Indies" class="mw-redirect" title="Federation of the West Indies">Federation of the West Indies</a>, a short-lived federation of <a href="/wiki/British_West_Indies" title="British West Indies">British West Indian colonies</a>. On 3 March 1967, it was granted full autonomy over its internal affairs as an <a href="/wiki/Associated_state" title="Associated state">associated state</a>. </p>
      <p>Independence was granted on 7 February 1974 under the leadership of <a href="/wiki/Eric_Gairy" title="Eric Gairy">Eric Gairy</a>, who became the first <a href="/wiki/List_of_heads_of_government_of_Grenada" title="List of heads of government of Grenada">Prime Minister of Grenada</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Sovereign_state" title="Sovereign state">sovereign state</a>. The new country became a member of the Commonwealth, with Queen Elizabeth as Head of State.<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_World_Factbook_-_Grenada_8-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA_World_Factbook_-_Grenada-8">[8]</a></sup> In March 1979, the <a href="/wiki/Marxism%E2%80%93Leninism" title="Marxism–Leninism">Marxist–Leninist</a> <a href="/wiki/New_Jewel_Movement" title="New Jewel Movement">New Jewel Movement</a> overthrew Gairy's government in a <a href="/wiki/Bloodless_coup" class="mw-redirect" title="Bloodless coup">bloodless <i>coup d'état</i></a> and established the <a href="/wiki/People%27s_Revolutionary_Government_(Grenada)" title="People's Revolutionary Government (Grenada)">People's Revolutionary Government</a> (PRG), headed by <a href="/wiki/Maurice_Bishop" title="Maurice Bishop">Maurice Bishop</a> as Prime Minister.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup> Bishop was later arrested and executed by members of the People's Revolutionary Army, prompting a <a href="/wiki/United_States_invasion_of_Grenada" title="United States invasion of Grenada">U.S.-led invasion</a> in October 1983. Since then, the island has remained politically stable without any further seizures of power.<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_World_Factbook_-_Grenada_8-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA_World_Factbook_-_Grenada-8">[8]</a></sup> </p>

      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology">Etymology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Grenada&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Etymology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <p>The origin of the name "Grenada" is obscure, but it is likely that Spanish sailors named the island for the <a href="/wiki/Andalusia" title="Andalusia">Andalusian</a> city of <a href="/wiki/Granada" title="Granada">Granada</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_World_Factbook_-_Grenada_8-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA_World_Factbook_-_Grenada-8">[8]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-:0_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-11">[11]</a></sup> It carried at least two other names during the <a href="/wiki/Age_of_Discovery" title="Age of Discovery">Age of Discovery</a>. </p>
      <p>On his <a href="/wiki/Voyages_of_Christopher_Columbus" title="Voyages of Christopher Columbus">third voyage</a> to the region in 1498, <a href="/wiki/Christopher_Columbus" title="Christopher Columbus">Christopher Columbus</a> sighted Grenada and named it "La Concepción" in honour of the <a href="/wiki/Mary,_mother_of_Jesus" title="Mary, mother of Jesus">Virgin Mary</a>. It is said that he may have actually named it "Assumpción", but it is uncertain, as he is said to have sighted what are now Grenada and Tobago from a distance and named them both at the same time. However, it became accepted that he named Tobago "Assumpción" and Grenada "La Concepción".<sup id="cite_ref-:0_11-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-11">[11]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In 1499, the Italian explorer <a href="/wiki/Amerigo_Vespucci" title="Amerigo Vespucci">Amerigo Vespucci</a> traveled through the region with the Spanish explorer <a href="/wiki/Alonso_de_Ojeda" title="Alonso de Ojeda">Alonso de Ojeda</a> and mapmaker <a href="/wiki/Juan_de_la_Cosa" title="Juan de la Cosa">Juan de la Cosa</a>. Vespucci is reported to have renamed the island "Mayo", although this is the only map where the name appears.<sup id="cite_ref-:1_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-12">[12]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>However, by the 1520s, Spanish maps used the name "Granada", and referred to the islands to the north as <i>Los Granadillos</i> ("Little Granadas").<sup id="cite_ref-grenada-french_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-grenada-french-13">[13]</a></sup> Although it was deemed the property of the <a href="/wiki/Monarchy_of_Spain" title="Monarchy of Spain">King of Spain</a>, there are no records to suggest the Spanish ever attempted to settle Grenada.<sup id="cite_ref-:1_12-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-12">[12]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The French maintained the name ("La Grenade" in French) after settlement and colonisation in 1649.<sup id="cite_ref-grenada-french_13-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-grenada-french-13">[13]</a></sup> On 10 February 1763, the island of La Grenade was ceded to the British under the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Paris_(1763)" title="Treaty of Paris (1763)">Treaty of Paris</a>. The British renamed it "Grenada", one of many place-name <a href="/wiki/Anglicisation" title="Anglicisation">anglicisations</a> they made there.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Grenada&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Grenada" title="History of Grenada">History of Grenada</a>
      </div> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Geological_history">Geological history</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Grenada&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Geological history">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>Approximately 2 million years ago in the <a href="/wiki/Pliocene" title="Pliocene">Pliocene</a> era, the area of what is nowadays Grenada emerged from a <a href="/wiki/Shallow_sea" class="mw-redirect" title="Shallow sea">shallow sea</a> as a submarine volcano. In recent times, <a href="/wiki/Volcanism" title="Volcanism">volcanic activity</a> has been non-existent, except for some of its <a href="/wiki/Hot_spring" title="Hot spring">hot spring</a> and under water volcano <a href="/wiki/Kick_%27em_Jenny" title="Kick 'em Jenny">Kick 'em Jenny</a>. Most of Grenada's terrain is made up from Volcanic Activity that would have taken place 1-2 million years ago.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2021)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> There would have been many unknown volcanoes responsible for the formation of Grenada including Grenada's capital <a href="/wiki/St._George%27s,_Grenada" title="St. George's, Grenada">St. Georges</a> with its horseshoe shaped harbour, the carenage. Two Non Existent Volcanoes which are now crater lakes, <a href="/wiki/Grand_Etang_Lake" title="Grand Etang Lake">Grand Etang Lake</a> and <a href="/w/index.php?title=Lake_Antoine,_Grenada&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Lake Antoine, Grenada (page does not exist)">Lake Antoine</a> would have also contributed towards the formation of Grenada. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Pre-Columbian_history">Pre-Columbian history</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Grenada&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Pre-Columbian history">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>Grenada was first populated by peoples from South America, possibly during the Caribbean <a href="/wiki/Ortoiroid_people" title="Ortoiroid people">Archaic Age</a>, although definitive evidence is lacking. The earliest potential human presence comes from <a href="/wiki/Proxy_(statistics)" title="Proxy (statistics)">proxy</a> evidence of lake cores, beginning ~3600 BC.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup> Less ephemeral, permanent villages began around ~AD 300.<sup id="cite_ref-Hanna_Camerhogne_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hanna_Camerhogne-16">[16]</a></sup> The population peaked between AD 750–1250, with major changes in population afterwards, potentially the result of regional droughts and/or the <a href="/wiki/Island_Caribs" class="mw-redirect" title="Island Caribs">"Carib Invasion"</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Hanna_Guianas_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hanna_Guianas-17">[17]</a></sup> although the latter rests on highly circumstantial evidence.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="European_arrival">European arrival</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Grenada&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: European arrival">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>It is thought that <a href="/wiki/Christopher_Columbus" title="Christopher Columbus">Christopher Columbus</a> was the first European to see Grenada in 1498 during his <a href="/wiki/Voyages_of_Christopher_Columbus" title="Voyages of Christopher Columbus">third voyage</a>, naming it 'Concepción'.<sup id="cite_ref-Encyclopedia_Britannica_-_Grenada_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Encyclopedia_Britannica_-_Grenada-19">[19]</a></sup> The Spanish did not follow up on this and it was the English who were the first to attempt to colonise the island in 1609; however they were driven away by the native Carib peoples.<sup id="cite_ref-Encyclopedia_Britannica_-_Grenada_19-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Encyclopedia_Britannica_-_Grenada-19">[19]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Steele,_pp._35–36_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Steele,_pp._35–36-20">[20]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-About_Grenada:_Historical_Events_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-About_Grenada:_Historical_Events-21">[21]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span id="French_colony_.281649.E2.80.931763.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="French_colony_(1649–1763)">French colony (1649–1763)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Grenada&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: French colony (1649–1763)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/French_West_Indies" title="French West Indies">French West Indies</a>
      </div> 
      <p>In 1649 a French expedition of 203 men from <a href="/wiki/Martinique" title="Martinique">Martinique</a> led by <a href="/wiki/Jacques_Dyel_du_Parquet" title="Jacques Dyel du Parquet">Jacques Dyel du Parquet</a> founded a permanent settlement on Grenada.<sup id="cite_ref-Encyclopedia_Britannica_-_Grenada_19-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Encyclopedia_Britannica_-_Grenada-19">[19]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Steele,_pp._35–36_20-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Steele,_pp._35–36-20">[20]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-About_Grenada:_Historical_Events_21-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-About_Grenada:_Historical_Events-21">[21]</a></sup> They signed a peace treaty with the Carib chief <a href="/wiki/Chief_Kairouane" title="Chief Kairouane">Kairouane</a>, but within months conflict broke out between the two communities.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup> This lasted until 1654 when the island was completely subjugated by the French.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup> The indigenous peoples who survived either left for neighbouring islands or retreated to remoter parts of Grenada, where they ultimately disappeared during the 1700s.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Warfare continued during the 1600s between the French on Grenada and the Caribs of present-day <a href="/wiki/Dominica" title="Dominica">Dominica</a> and <a href="/wiki/St._Vincent_and_the_Grenadines" class="mw-redirect" title="St. Vincent and the Grenadines">St. Vincent and the Grenadines</a>. </p>
      <p>The French named their <a href="/wiki/French_colonial_empires" class="mw-redirect" title="French colonial empires">new colony</a> La Grenade, and the economy was initially based on <a href="/wiki/Sugar_cane" class="mw-redirect" title="Sugar cane">sugar cane</a> and <a href="/wiki/Indigo" title="Indigo">indigo</a>, worked by African slaves.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup> The French established a capital known as <a href="/wiki/St_George%27s,_Grenada" class="mw-redirect" title="St George's, Grenada">Fort Royal</a> (later St. George's). To shelter from hurricanes the French navy would often take refuge in the capital's natural harbour, as no nearby French islands had a natural harbour to compare with that of Fort Royal. The British captured Grenada during the <a href="/wiki/Seven_Years%27_War" title="Seven Years' War">Seven Years' War</a> in 1762.<sup id="cite_ref-Encyclopedia_Britannica_-_Grenada_19-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Encyclopedia_Britannica_-_Grenada-19">[19]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="British_colonial_period">British colonial period</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Grenada&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: British colonial period">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Port_Saint-Georges_dans_l%27%C3%AEle_de_la_Grenade_en_1776.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/Port_Saint-Georges_dans_l%27%C3%AEle_de_la_Grenade_en_1776.jpg/220px-Port_Saint-Georges_dans_l%27%C3%AEle_de_la_Grenade_en_1776.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="123" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/Port_Saint-Georges_dans_l%27%C3%AEle_de_la_Grenade_en_1776.jpg/330px-Port_Saint-Georges_dans_l%27%C3%AEle_de_la_Grenade_en_1776.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/Port_Saint-Georges_dans_l%27%C3%AEle_de_la_Grenade_en_1776.jpg/440px-Port_Saint-Georges_dans_l%27%C3%AEle_de_la_Grenade_en_1776.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1276" data-file-height="715"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Port_Saint-Georges_dans_l%27%C3%AEle_de_la_Grenade_en_1776.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The island of Grenada and port Saint-Georges in 1776.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_colonial_period">Early colonial period</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Grenada&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Early colonial period">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/British_West_Indies" title="British West Indies">British West Indies</a>, <a href="/wiki/British_Windward_Islands" title="British Windward Islands">British Windward Islands</a>, and <a href="/wiki/West_Indies_Federation" title="West Indies Federation">West Indies Federation</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Grenada was formally ceded to <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Great_Britain" title="Kingdom of Great Britain">Britain</a> by the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Paris_(1763)" title="Treaty of Paris (1763)">Treaty of Paris</a> in 1763.<sup id="cite_ref-Encyclopedia_Britannica_-_Grenada_19-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Encyclopedia_Britannica_-_Grenada-19">[19]</a></sup> The French <a href="/wiki/French_capture_of_Grenada_1779" class="mw-redirect" title="French capture of Grenada 1779">re-captured the island</a> during the <a href="/wiki/American_Revolutionary_War" title="American Revolutionary War">American Revolutionary War</a>, after <a href="/wiki/Comte_d%27Estaing" class="mw-redirect" title="Comte d'Estaing">Comte d'Estaing</a> won the bloody land and naval <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Grenada" title="Battle of Grenada">Battle of Grenada</a> in July 1779.<sup id="cite_ref-Encyclopedia_Britannica_-_Grenada_19-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Encyclopedia_Britannica_-_Grenada-19">[19]</a></sup> However the island was restored to Britain with the <a href="/wiki/Peace_of_Paris_(1783)" title="Peace of Paris (1783)">Treaty of Versailles</a> in 1783.<sup id="cite_ref-Encyclopedia_Britannica_-_Grenada_19-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Encyclopedia_Britannica_-_Grenada-19">[19]</a></sup> A decade later dissatisfaction with British rule led to a <a href="/wiki/F%C3%A9don_Rebellion" class="mw-redirect" title="Fédon Rebellion">pro-French revolt</a> in 1795–96 led by <a href="/wiki/Julien_F%C3%A9don" title="Julien Fédon">Julien Fédon</a>, which was successfully defeated by the British.<sup id="cite_ref-cavehill_26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cavehill-26">[26]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>As Grenada's economy grew, more and more African slaves were forcibly transported to the island. Britain eventually outlawed the slave trade within the British Empire in 1807, and slavery was completely outlawed in 1833, leading to the emancipation of all enslaved by 1838.<sup id="cite_ref-Encyclopedia_Britannica_-_Grenada_19-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Encyclopedia_Britannica_-_Grenada-19">[19]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup> In an effort to ameliorate the subsequent labour shortage, migrants from India were brought to Grenada in 1857.<sup id="cite_ref-Steele,_pp._35–36_20-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Steele,_pp._35–36-20">[20]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-About_Grenada:_Historical_Events_21-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-About_Grenada:_Historical_Events-21">[21]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-hisfacts_29-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hisfacts-29">[29]</a></sup> </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Nutmeg" title="Nutmeg">Nutmeg</a> was introduced to Grenada in 1843 when a merchant ship called in on its way to England from the East Indies.<sup id="cite_ref-Steele,_pp._35–36_20-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Steele,_pp._35–36-20">[20]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-About_Grenada:_Historical_Events_21-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-About_Grenada:_Historical_Events-21">[21]</a></sup> The ship had a small quantity of nutmeg trees on board which they left in Grenada, and this was the beginning of Grenada's nutmeg industry that now supplies nearly 40% of the world's annual crop.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Later_colonial_period">Later colonial period</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Grenada&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Later colonial period">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Eric_Gairy.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/ad/Eric_Gairy.jpg/220px-Eric_Gairy.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="228" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/a/ad/Eric_Gairy.jpg 1.5x" data-file-width="300" data-file-height="311"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Eric_Gairy.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Eric Gairy, first Prime Minister of Grenada
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>In 1877 Grenada was made a <a href="/wiki/Crown_colony" title="Crown colony">Crown colony</a>. <a href="/wiki/Theophilus_A._Marryshow" class="mw-redirect" title="Theophilus A. Marryshow">Theophilus A. Marryshow</a> founded the Representative Government Association (RGA) in 1917 to agitate for a new and participative constitutional dispensation for the Grenadian people.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Partly as a result of Marryshow's lobbying, the Wood Commission of 1921–22 concluded that Grenada was ready for constitutional reform in the form of a modified Crown colony government. This modification granted Grenadians the right to elect five of the 15 members of the Legislative Council, on a restricted property franchise enabling the wealthiest 4% of adult Grenadians to vote.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup> Marryshow was named a <a href="/wiki/1943_Birthday_Honours#Commander_of_the_Order_of_the_British_Empire_(CBE)" title="1943 Birthday Honours">Commander of the Order of the British Empire (CBE) in 1943</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p>
      <p>In 1950 <a href="/wiki/Eric_Gairy" title="Eric Gairy">Eric Gairy</a> founded the <a href="/wiki/Grenada_United_Labour_Party" title="Grenada United Labour Party">Grenada United Labour Party</a> (GULP), initially as a trade union, which led the 1951 <a href="/wiki/General_strike" title="General strike">general strike</a> for better working conditions.<sup id="cite_ref-Steele,_pp._35–36_20-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Steele,_pp._35–36-20">[20]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-About_Grenada:_Historical_Events_21-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-About_Grenada:_Historical_Events-21">[21]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup> This sparked great unrest—so many buildings were set ablaze that the disturbances became known as the "red sky" days—and the British authorities decided to call in military reinforcements to help regain control of the situation.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> On 10 October 1951, Grenada held its <a href="/wiki/1951_Grenadian_general_election" title="1951 Grenadian general election">first general elections</a> on the basis of universal adult suffrage,<sup id="cite_ref-bigdrumnation.org_33-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bigdrumnation.org-33">[33]</a></sup> with Gairy's party winning six of the eight seats contested.<sup id="cite_ref-bigdrumnation.org_33-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bigdrumnation.org-33">[33]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>From 1958 to 1962 Grenada was part of the <a href="/wiki/Federation_of_the_West_Indies" class="mw-redirect" title="Federation of the West Indies">Federation of the West Indies</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Encyclopedia_Britannica_-_Grenada_19-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Encyclopedia_Britannica_-_Grenada-19">[19]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Steele,_pp._35–36_20-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Steele,_pp._35–36-20">[20]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-About_Grenada:_Historical_Events_21-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-About_Grenada:_Historical_Events-21">[21]</a></sup> After the federation's collapse Grenada was granted full autonomy over its internal affairs as an Associated State on 3 March 1967.<sup id="cite_ref-Encyclopedia_Britannica_-_Grenada_19-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Encyclopedia_Britannica_-_Grenada-19">[19]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Herbert_Blaize" title="Herbert Blaize">Herbert Blaize</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Grenada_National_Party" title="Grenada National Party">Grenada National Party</a> (GNP) was the first Premier of the Associated State of Grenada from March to August 1967. Eric Gairy served as <a href="/wiki/Premier_of_Grenada" class="mw-redirect" title="Premier of Grenada">Premier</a> from August 1967 until February 1974.<sup id="cite_ref-Encyclopedia_Britannica_-_Grenada_19-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Encyclopedia_Britannica_-_Grenada-19">[19]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Post-independence_era">Post-independence era</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Grenada&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Post-independence era">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Bundesarchiv_Bild_183-1982-0610-101,_Berlin,_Besuch_Regierungsdelegation_Grenada,_Bootsfahrt.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ca/Bundesarchiv_Bild_183-1982-0610-101%2C_Berlin%2C_Besuch_Regierungsdelegation_Grenada%2C_Bootsfahrt.jpg/220px-Bundesarchiv_Bild_183-1982-0610-101%2C_Berlin%2C_Besuch_Regierungsdelegation_Grenada%2C_Bootsfahrt.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="142" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ca/Bundesarchiv_Bild_183-1982-0610-101%2C_Berlin%2C_Besuch_Regierungsdelegation_Grenada%2C_Bootsfahrt.jpg/330px-Bundesarchiv_Bild_183-1982-0610-101%2C_Berlin%2C_Besuch_Regierungsdelegation_Grenada%2C_Bootsfahrt.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ca/Bundesarchiv_Bild_183-1982-0610-101%2C_Berlin%2C_Besuch_Regierungsdelegation_Grenada%2C_Bootsfahrt.jpg/440px-Bundesarchiv_Bild_183-1982-0610-101%2C_Berlin%2C_Besuch_Regierungsdelegation_Grenada%2C_Bootsfahrt.jpg 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="515"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Bundesarchiv_Bild_183-1982-0610-101,_Berlin,_Besuch_Regierungsdelegation_Grenada,_Bootsfahrt.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Maurice_Bishop" title="Maurice Bishop">Maurice Bishop</a> visiting East Germany, 1982
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Independence was granted on 7 February 1974, under the leadership of Eric Gairy, who became the first <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_Grenada" class="mw-redirect" title="Prime Minister of Grenada">Prime Minister of Grenada</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Encyclopedia_Britannica_-_Grenada_19-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Encyclopedia_Britannica_-_Grenada-19">[19]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Steele,_pp._35–36_20-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Steele,_pp._35–36-20">[20]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-About_Grenada:_Historical_Events_21-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-About_Grenada:_Historical_Events-21">[21]</a></sup> Grenada opted to remain within the <a href="/wiki/British_Commonwealth" class="mw-redirect" title="British Commonwealth">British Commonwealth</a>, retaining Queen Elizabeth as <a href="/wiki/Monarchy_of_Grenada" title="Monarchy of Grenada">Monarch</a>, represented locally by a <a href="/wiki/Governor-General_of_Grenada" title="Governor-General of Grenada">Governor-General</a>. Civil conflict gradually broke out between Eric Gairy's government and some opposition parties, including the Marxist <a href="/wiki/New_Jewel_Movement" title="New Jewel Movement">New Jewel Movement</a> (NJM).<sup id="cite_ref-Encyclopedia_Britannica_-_Grenada_19-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Encyclopedia_Britannica_-_Grenada-19">[19]</a></sup> Gairy and the GULP won the <a href="/wiki/1976_Grenadian_general_election" title="1976 Grenadian general election">1976 Grenadian general election</a>, albeit with a reduced majority;<sup id="cite_ref-Encyclopedia_Britannica_-_Grenada_19-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Encyclopedia_Britannica_-_Grenada-19">[19]</a></sup> however the opposition deemed the results invalid due to fraud and the violent intimidation performed by the so-called '<a href="/wiki/Mongoose_Gang" title="Mongoose Gang">Mongoose Gang</a>', a private militia loyal to Gairy.<sup id="cite_ref-N1_34-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-N1-34">[34]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>On 13 March 1979, whilst Gairy was out of the country, the NJM launched a <a href="/wiki/Bloodless_coup" class="mw-redirect" title="Bloodless coup">bloodless coup</a> which removed Gairy, suspended the constitution, and established a <a href="/wiki/People%27s_Revolutionary_Government" class="mw-redirect" title="People's Revolutionary Government">People's Revolutionary Government</a> (PRG), headed by <a href="/wiki/Maurice_Bishop" title="Maurice Bishop">Maurice Bishop</a> who declared himself Prime Minister.<sup id="cite_ref-Encyclopedia_Britannica_-_Grenada_19-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Encyclopedia_Britannica_-_Grenada-19">[19]</a></sup> His <a href="/wiki/Marxism%E2%80%93Leninism" title="Marxism–Leninism">Marxist–Leninist</a> government established close ties with <a href="/wiki/Cuba" title="Cuba">Cuba</a>, Nicaragua, and other <a href="/wiki/Communist_bloc" class="mw-redirect" title="Communist bloc">communist bloc</a> countries.<sup id="cite_ref-Encyclopedia_Britannica_-_Grenada_19-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Encyclopedia_Britannica_-_Grenada-19">[19]</a></sup> All political parties except for the New Jewel Movement were banned and no elections were held during the four years of PRG rule. </p> 
      <h3><span id="Invasion_by_the_United_States_.281983.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Invasion_by_the_United_States_(1983)">Invasion by the United States (1983)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Grenada&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Invasion by the United States (1983)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/United_States_invasion_of_Grenada" title="United States invasion of Grenada">United States invasion of Grenada</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Eastern_Caribbean_Defense_Force.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/Eastern_Caribbean_Defense_Force.jpg/220px-Eastern_Caribbean_Defense_Force.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="142" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/Eastern_Caribbean_Defense_Force.jpg/330px-Eastern_Caribbean_Defense_Force.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/Eastern_Caribbean_Defense_Force.jpg/440px-Eastern_Caribbean_Defense_Force.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3020" data-file-height="1950"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Eastern_Caribbean_Defense_Force.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Members of the Eastern Caribbean Defence Force during the 1983 <a href="/wiki/Invasion_of_Grenada" class="mw-redirect" title="Invasion of Grenada">invasion of Grenada</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Coup_and_execution_of_Maurice_Bishop">Coup and execution of Maurice Bishop</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Grenada&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Coup and execution of Maurice Bishop">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <p>Some years later a dispute developed between Bishop and certain high-ranking members of the NJM. Though Bishop cooperated with <a href="/wiki/Cuba" title="Cuba">Cuba</a> and the <a href="/wiki/USSR" class="mw-redirect" title="USSR">USSR</a> on various trade and foreign policy issues, he sought to maintain a "non-aligned" status. Bishop had been taking his time making Grenada wholly <a href="/wiki/Socialist" class="mw-redirect" title="Socialist">socialist</a>, simultaneously encouraging private-sector development in an attempt to make the island a popular tourist destination.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Hardline <a href="/wiki/Marxist" class="mw-redirect" title="Marxist">Marxist</a> party members, including <a href="/wiki/Communist" class="mw-redirect" title="Communist">communist</a> Deputy Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Bernard_Coard" title="Bernard Coard">Bernard Coard</a>, deemed Bishop insufficiently revolutionary and demanded that he either step down or enter into a power-sharing arrangement. </p>
      <p>On 16 October 1983 Bernard Coard and his wife, Phyllis, backed by the Grenadian Army, led a coup against the government of Maurice Bishop and placed Bishop under <a href="/wiki/House_arrest" title="House arrest">house arrest</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Encyclopedia_Britannica_-_Grenada_19-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Encyclopedia_Britannica_-_Grenada-19">[19]</a></sup> These actions led to street demonstrations in various parts of the island because Bishop had widespread support from the population. Because Bishop was a widely popular leader, he was freed by impassioned supporters who marched en masse on his guarded residence from a rally in the capital's central square. Bishop then led the crowd to the island's military headquarters to reassert his power. Grenadian soldiers were dispatched in armored vehicles by the Coard faction to retake the fort. A confrontation between soldiers and civilians at the fort ended in gunfire and panic. Three soldiers and at least eight civilians died in the tumult that also injured 100 others, a school-sponsored study later found.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Avoid_weasel_words" class="mw-redirect" title="Wikipedia:Avoid weasel words"><span title="The material near this tag possibly uses too vague attribution or weasel words. (March 2021)">which?</span></a></i>]</sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Dates_and_numbers#Chronological_items" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Dates and numbers"><span title="The time period mentioned near this tag is ambiguous. (March 2021)">when?</span></a></i>]</sup> When the initial shooting ended with Bishop's surrender, he and seven of his closest supporters were taken prisoner and executed by a firing squad of soldiers. Besides Bishop, the group included three of his cabinet ministers, a trade union leader and three service-industry workers.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify"><span title="were the cabinet ministers the executors or the executees? (December 2018)">clarification needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p>
      <p>After the execution of Bishop, the <a href="/wiki/People%27s_Revolutionary_Army_(Grenada)" title="People's Revolutionary Army (Grenada)">People's Revolutionary Army</a> (PRA) formed a military Marxist government with General <a href="/wiki/Hudson_Austin" title="Hudson Austin">Hudson Austin</a> as chairman. The army declared a four-day total curfew, during which anyone leaving their home without approval would be shot on sight.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="United_States_and_allied_response_and_reaction">United States and allied response and reaction</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Grenada&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: United States and allied response and reaction">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:M102_howitzers_during_Operation_Urgent_Fury.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/M102_howitzers_during_Operation_Urgent_Fury.jpg/220px-M102_howitzers_during_Operation_Urgent_Fury.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="150" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/M102_howitzers_during_Operation_Urgent_Fury.jpg/330px-M102_howitzers_during_Operation_Urgent_Fury.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/M102_howitzers_during_Operation_Urgent_Fury.jpg/440px-M102_howitzers_during_Operation_Urgent_Fury.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2920" data-file-height="1990"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:M102_howitzers_during_Operation_Urgent_Fury.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>M102 howitzers of <a href="/wiki/320th_Field_Artillery_Regiment" title="320th Field Artillery Regiment">320th Field Artillery Regiment</a> firing during the 1983 <a href="/wiki/Invasion_of_Grenada" class="mw-redirect" title="Invasion of Grenada">invasion of Grenada</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>US President <a href="/wiki/Ronald_Reagan" title="Ronald Reagan">Ronald Reagan</a> stated that particularly worrying was the presence of Cuban construction workers and military personnel building a 10,000-foot (3,000&nbsp;m) <a href="/wiki/Point_Salines_International_Airport" class="mw-redirect" title="Point Salines International Airport">airstrip</a> on Grenada.<sup id="cite_ref-Gailey_39-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gailey-39">[39]</a></sup> Bishop had stated the purpose of the airstrip was to allow commercial jets to land, but some US military analysts argued that the only reason for constructing such a long and reinforced runway was so that it could be used by heavy military transport planes. The contractors, American and European companies, and the <a href="/wiki/European_Economic_Community" title="European Economic Community">EEC</a>, which provided partial funding, all claimed the airstrip did not have military capabilities.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2021)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Reagan claimed that Cuba, under the direction of the Soviet Union, would use Grenada as a refuelling stop for Cuban and Soviet airplanes loaded with weapons destined for Central American communist insurgents.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The Organization of Eastern Caribbean States (OECS), Barbados, and Jamaica all appealed to the United States for assistance.<sup id="cite_ref-dtic_41-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dtic-41">[41]</a></sup> On 25 October 1983, combined forces from the United States and from the <a href="/wiki/Regional_Security_System" title="Regional Security System">Regional Security System</a> (RSS) based in <a href="/wiki/Barbados" title="Barbados">Barbados</a> invaded Grenada in an operation codenamed <i><a href="/wiki/Invasion_of_Grenada" class="mw-redirect" title="Invasion of Grenada">Operation Urgent Fury</a></i>. The US stated this was done at the behest of Barbados, <a href="/wiki/Dominica" title="Dominica">Dominica</a><sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> and <a href="/wiki/Governor-General_of_Grenada" title="Governor-General of Grenada">Governor-General of Grenada</a>, <a href="/wiki/Paul_Scoon" title="Paul Scoon">Sir Paul Scoon</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup> Scoon had requested the invasion through secret diplomatic channels, but it was not made public for his safety.<sup id="cite_ref-z9f6WdltuE_43-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-z9f6WdltuE-43">[43]</a></sup> Progress was rapid and within four days the Americans had removed the military government of <a href="/wiki/Hudson_Austin" title="Hudson Austin">Hudson Austin</a>. </p>
      <p>The invasion was heavily criticized by the governments of Britain,<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Trinidad_and_Tobago" title="Trinidad and Tobago">Trinidad and Tobago</a>, and Canada. The <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_General_Assembly" title="United Nations General Assembly">United Nations General Assembly</a> condemned it as "a flagrant violation of international law" by a vote of 108 in favor to 9, with 27 abstentions.<sup id="cite_ref-UN_Resolution_45-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UN_Resolution-45">[45]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-UN_Resolution_Vote_46-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UN_Resolution_Vote-46">[46]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Security_Council" title="United Nations Security Council">United Nations Security Council</a> considered a similar resolution, which was supported by 11 nations. However, the United States vetoed the motion.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Post-invasion_arrests">Post-invasion arrests</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Grenada&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Post-invasion arrests">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <p>After the invasion, the pre-revolutionary Grenadian constitution came into operation once again. Eighteen members of the PRG/PRA were arrested on charges related to the murder of Maurice Bishop and seven others. The 18 included the top political leadership of Grenada at the time of the execution, along with the entire military chain of command directly responsible for the operation that led to the executions. Fourteen were <a href="/wiki/Capital_punishment" title="Capital punishment">sentenced to death</a>, one was found not guilty, and three were sentenced to 45 years in prison. The death sentences were eventually commuted to terms of imprisonment. Those in prison have become known as 'the <a href="/wiki/Grenada_17" title="Grenada 17">Grenada 17</a>'.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Grenada_since_1983">Grenada since 1983</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Grenada&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Grenada since 1983">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>When US troops withdrew from Grenada in December 1983, <a href="/wiki/Nicholas_Brathwaite" title="Nicholas Brathwaite">Nicholas Brathwaite</a> of the <a href="/wiki/National_Democratic_Congress_(Grenada)" title="National Democratic Congress (Grenada)">National Democratic Congress</a> was appointed Prime Minister of an interim administration by Governor-General Scoon until elections could be organised.<sup id="cite_ref-Encyclopedia_Britannica_-_Grenada_19-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Encyclopedia_Britannica_-_Grenada-19">[19]</a></sup> The first democratic elections since 1976 were <a href="/wiki/1984_Grenadian_general_election" title="1984 Grenadian general election">held in December 1984</a>, and were won by the <a href="/wiki/Grenada_National_Party" title="Grenada National Party">Grenada National Party</a> under <a href="/wiki/Herbert_Blaize" title="Herbert Blaize">Herbert Blaize</a>, who served as Prime Minister until his death in December 1989.<sup id="cite_ref-PP_49-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PP-49">[49]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Jan_50-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Jan-50">[50]</a></sup> </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Ben_Jones_(Grenada)" class="mw-redirect" title="Ben Jones (Grenada)">Ben Jones</a> briefly succeeded Blaize as Prime Minister and served until the <a href="/wiki/1990_Grenadian_general_election" title="1990 Grenadian general election">March 1990 election</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-GovGrenada_52-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GovGrenada-52">[52]</a></sup> which was won by the National Democratic Congress under Nicholas Brathwaite who returned as Prime Minister for a second time until he resigned in February 1995.<sup id="cite_ref-jo_53-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-jo-53">[53]</a></sup> He was succeeded by <a href="/wiki/George_Brizan" title="George Brizan">George Brizan</a> who served for a brief period<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup> until the <a href="/wiki/1995_Grenadian_general_election" title="1995 Grenadian general election">June 1995 election</a> which was won by the <a href="/wiki/New_National_Party_(Grenada)" title="New National Party (Grenada)">New National Party</a> under <a href="/wiki/Keith_Mitchell" title="Keith Mitchell">Keith Mitchell</a>, who went on to win the <a href="/wiki/1999_Grenadian_general_election" title="1999 Grenadian general election">1999</a> and 2003 elections, serving for a record 13 years until 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-Encyclopedia_Britannica_-_Grenada_19-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Encyclopedia_Britannica_-_Grenada-19">[19]</a></sup> Mitchell re-established relations with <a href="/wiki/Cuba" title="Cuba">Cuba</a> and also reformed the country's banking system, which had come in for criticism over potential money laundering concerns.<sup id="cite_ref-Encyclopedia_Britannica_-_Grenada_19-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Encyclopedia_Britannica_-_Grenada-19">[19]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Steele,_pp._35–36_20-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Steele,_pp._35–36-20">[20]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-About_Grenada:_Historical_Events_21-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-About_Grenada:_Historical_Events-21">[21]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In 2000–02, much of the controversy of the late 1970s and early 1980s was once again brought into the public consciousness with the opening of the <a href="/wiki/Truth_and_reconciliation_commission" class="mw-redirect" title="Truth and reconciliation commission">truth and reconciliation commission</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Encyclopedia_Britannica_-_Grenada_19-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Encyclopedia_Britannica_-_Grenada-19">[19]</a></sup> The commission was chaired by a <a href="/wiki/Holy_Orders" class="mw-redirect" title="Holy Orders">Roman Catholic priest</a>, Father Mark Haynes, and was tasked with uncovering injustices arising from the PRA, Bishop's regime, and before. It held a number of hearings around the country. Brother Robert Fanovich, head of Presentation Brothers' College (PBC) in St. George's tasked some of his senior students with conducting a research project into the era and specifically into the fact that Maurice Bishop's body was never discovered.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup> Paterson also uncovered that there was still a lot of resentment in Grenadian society resulting from the era and a feeling that there were many injustices still unaddressed.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:277px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Grenada_ivan.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/Grenada_ivan.jpg/275px-Grenada_ivan.jpg" decoding="async" width="275" height="161" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/4/4b/Grenada_ivan.jpg 1.5x" data-file-width="300" data-file-height="176"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Grenada_ivan.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Aftermath of Hurricane Ivan in Grenada
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>On 7 September 2004, after being hurricane-free for 49 years, the island was directly hit by <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Ivan" title="Hurricane Ivan">Hurricane Ivan</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup> Ivan struck as a <a href="/wiki/Saffir-Simpson_Hurricane_Scale" class="mw-redirect" title="Saffir-Simpson Hurricane Scale">Category 3 hurricane</a>, resulting in 39 deaths and damage or destruction to 90% of the island's homes.<sup id="cite_ref-Encyclopedia_Britannica_-_Grenada_19-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Encyclopedia_Britannica_-_Grenada-19">[19]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Steele,_pp._35–36_20-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Steele,_pp._35–36-20">[20]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-About_Grenada:_Historical_Events_21-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-About_Grenada:_Historical_Events-21">[21]</a></sup> On 14 July 2005, <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Emily_(2005)" title="Hurricane Emily (2005)">Hurricane Emily</a>, a Category 1 hurricane at the time, struck the northern part of the island with 80-knot (150&nbsp;km/h; 92&nbsp;mph) winds, killing one person and causing an estimated US$110&nbsp;million (EC$297&nbsp;million) worth of damage.<sup id="cite_ref-Steele,_pp._35–36_20-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Steele,_pp._35–36-20">[20]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-About_Grenada:_Historical_Events_21-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-About_Grenada:_Historical_Events-21">[21]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-EmilyTCR_57-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EmilyTCR-57">[57]</a></sup> Agriculture, and in particular the <a href="/wiki/Nutmeg" title="Nutmeg">nutmeg</a> industry, suffered serious losses, but that event has begun changes in crop management and it is hoped that as new nutmeg trees mature, the industry will gradually rebuild. </p>
      <p>Mitchell was defeated in the <a href="/wiki/2008_Grenadian_general_election" title="2008 Grenadian general election">2008 election</a> by the NDC under <a href="/wiki/Tillman_Thomas" title="Tillman Thomas">Tillman Thomas</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-IHT_58-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IHT-58">[58]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Nation_59-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Nation-59">[59]</a></sup> however he won the <a href="/wiki/2013_Grenadian_general_election" title="2013 Grenadian general election">2013 Grenadian general election</a> by a landslide and the NNP returned to power,<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup> winning again by another landslide <a href="/wiki/2018_Grenadian_general_election" title="2018 Grenadian general election">in 2018</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup> In March 2020, <a href="/wiki/2020_coronavirus_pandemic_in_Grenada" class="mw-redirect" title="2020 coronavirus pandemic in Grenada">Grenada confirmed its first case of COVID-19</a>, of which the economic effects are expected to rival past downturns, including <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Ivan" title="Hurricane Ivan">Hurricane Ivan</a>. </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Grenada&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Geography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_Grenada" title="Geography of Grenada">Geography of Grenada</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Grenada-map.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/Grenada-map.png/250px-Grenada-map.png" decoding="async" width="250" height="310" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/Grenada-map.png/375px-Grenada-map.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/Grenada-map.png/500px-Grenada-map.png 2x" data-file-width="961" data-file-height="1191"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Grenada-map.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>A map of Grenada
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The island of Grenada is the southernmost island in the <a href="/wiki/Antilles" title="Antilles">Antilles</a> archipelago, bordering the eastern Caribbean Sea and western Atlantic Ocean, and roughly 140&nbsp;km (90&nbsp;mi) north of both <a href="/wiki/Venezuela" title="Venezuela">Venezuela</a> and <a href="/wiki/Trinidad_and_Tobago" title="Trinidad and Tobago">Trinidad and Tobago</a>. Its sister islands make up the southern section of <a href="/wiki/The_Grenadines" class="mw-redirect" title="The Grenadines">the Grenadines</a>, which include <a href="/wiki/Carriacou" title="Carriacou">Carriacou</a>, <a href="/wiki/Petite_Martinique" title="Petite Martinique">Petite Martinique</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ronde_Island" title="Ronde Island">Ronde Island</a>, <a href="/wiki/Caille_Island" title="Caille Island">Caille Island</a>, <a href="/wiki/Diamond_Island_(Grenadines)" title="Diamond Island (Grenadines)">Diamond Island</a>, <a href="/wiki/Large_Island" title="Large Island">Large Island</a>, <a href="/wiki/Saline_Island" title="Saline Island">Saline Island</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Frigate_Island,_Grenada" title="Frigate Island, Grenada">Frigate Island</a>; the remaining islands to the north belong to <a href="/wiki/St_Vincent_and_the_Grenadines" class="mw-redirect" title="St Vincent and the Grenadines">St Vincent and the Grenadines</a>. Most of the population lives on Grenada, and major towns there include the capital, <a href="/wiki/St._George%27s,_Grenada" title="St. George's, Grenada">St. George's</a>, <a href="/wiki/Grenville,_Grenada" title="Grenville, Grenada">Grenville</a> and <a href="/wiki/Gouyave" title="Gouyave">Gouyave</a>. The largest settlement on the sister islands is <a href="/wiki/Hillsborough,_Grenada" class="mw-redirect" title="Hillsborough, Grenada">Hillsborough</a> on <a href="/wiki/Carriacou" title="Carriacou">Carriacou</a>. </p>
      <p>Grenada is of <a href="/wiki/Volcanic" class="mw-redirect" title="Volcanic">volcanic</a> origin,<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_World_Factbook_-_Grenada_8-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA_World_Factbook_-_Grenada-8">[8]</a></sup> as evident in its soil, mountainous interior, and several explosion craters, including <a href="/w/index.php?title=Lake_Antoine,_Grenada&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Lake Antoine, Grenada (page does not exist)">Lake Antoine</a>, <a href="/wiki/Grand_Etang_Lake" title="Grand Etang Lake">Grand Etang Lake</a> and <a href="/w/index.php?title=Levera_Pond&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Levera Pond (page does not exist)">Levera Pond</a>. Grenada's highest point is <a href="/wiki/Mount_Saint_Catherine_(Grenada)" title="Mount Saint Catherine (Grenada)">Mount St. Catherine</a>, rising to 840&nbsp;m (2,760&nbsp;ft) above sea level.<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_World_Factbook_-_Grenada_8-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA_World_Factbook_-_Grenada-8">[8]</a></sup> Other major mountains include <a href="/w/index.php?title=Mount_Granby&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Mount Granby (page does not exist)">Mount Granby</a> and <a href="/w/index.php?title=South_East_Mountain&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="South East Mountain (page does not exist)">South East Mountain</a>. Several small rivers with waterfalls flow into the sea from these mountains. The coastline contains several bays, most notably on the southern coast which is split into numerous thin peninsulas. </p>
      <p>Grenada is home to four ecoregions: Windward Islands moist forests, Leeward Islands dry forests, Windward Islands dry forests, and Windward Islands xeric scrub.<sup id="cite_ref-DinersteinOlson2017_62-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DinersteinOlson2017-62">[62]</a></sup> It had a 2018 <a href="/wiki/Forest_Landscape_Integrity_Index" title="Forest Landscape Integrity Index">Forest Landscape Integrity Index</a> mean score of 4.22/10, ranking it 131st globally out of 172 countries.<sup id="cite_ref-FLII-Supplementary_63-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FLII-Supplementary-63">[63]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="center">
       <div class="thumb tnone">
        <div class="thumbinner" style="width:602px;">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Grenada2010.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c3/Grenada2010.jpg/600px-Grenada2010.jpg" decoding="async" width="600" height="400" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c3/Grenada2010.jpg/900px-Grenada2010.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c3/Grenada2010.jpg/1200px-Grenada2010.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2448" data-file-height="1632"></a> 
         <div class="thumbcaption">
          <div class="magnify">
           <a href="/wiki/File:Grenada2010.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
          </div>An aerial photo of the capital <a href="/wiki/St._George%27s,_Grenada" title="St. George's, Grenada">St. George's</a>
         </div>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Grenada&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Climate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Climate" title="Climate">climate</a> is tropical: hot and humid in the <a href="/wiki/Dry_season" title="Dry season">dry season</a> and cooled by the moderate rainfall in the <a href="/wiki/Rainy_season" class="mw-redirect" title="Rainy season">rainy season</a>. Temperatures range from 32&nbsp;°C-22&nbsp;°C (89&nbsp;°F-71&nbsp;°F) and is rarely below 18&nbsp;°C (68&nbsp;°F). Grenada, being on the southern edge of the <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_belt" class="mw-redirect" title="Hurricane belt">hurricane belt</a>, has suffered only three hurricanes in fifty years.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Janet" title="Hurricane Janet">Hurricane Janet</a> passed over Grenada on 23 September 1955, with winds of 185&nbsp;km/h (115&nbsp;mph), causing severe damage. The most recent storms to hit Grenada have been Hurricane Ivan on 7 September 2004, causing severe damage and thirty-nine deaths, and Hurricane Emily on 14 July 2005, causing serious damage in Carriacou and in the north of Grenada, which had been relatively lightly affected by Hurricane Ivan.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Politics">Politics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Grenada&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Politics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_Grenada" title="Politics of Grenada">Politics of Grenada</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Grenada is a <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_realm" title="Commonwealth realm">Commonwealth realm</a> with <a href="/wiki/Queen_Elizabeth_II" class="mw-redirect" title="Queen Elizabeth II">Queen Elizabeth II</a> as <a href="/wiki/Head_of_state" title="Head of state">head of state</a>, represented locally by a <a href="/wiki/List_of_Governors-General_of_Grenada" class="mw-redirect" title="List of Governors-General of Grenada">Governor-General</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_World_Factbook_-_Grenada_8-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA_World_Factbook_-_Grenada-8">[8]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Encyclopedia_Britannica_-_Grenada_19-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Encyclopedia_Britannica_-_Grenada-19">[19]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Executive_(government)" title="Executive (government)">Executive power</a> lies with the head of government, the <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_Grenada" class="mw-redirect" title="Prime Minister of Grenada">Prime Minister</a>. The Governor-General role is largely ceremonial, while the Prime Minister is usually the leader of the largest party in <a href="/wiki/Parliament_of_Grenada" title="Parliament of Grenada">Parliament</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_World_Factbook_-_Grenada_8-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA_World_Factbook_-_Grenada-8">[8]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The Parliament of Grenada consists of a Senate (13 members) and a House of Representatives (15 members). Senators are appointed by the government and the opposition, while the Representatives are elected by the population for five-year terms.<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_World_Factbook_-_Grenada_8-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA_World_Factbook_-_Grenada-8">[8]</a></sup> Grenada operates a multi-party system, with the largest parties being the centre-right <a href="/wiki/New_National_Party_(Grenada)" title="New National Party (Grenada)">New National Party</a> (NNP) and the centre-left <a href="/wiki/National_Democratic_Congress_(Grenada)" title="National Democratic Congress (Grenada)">National Democratic Congress</a> (NDC).<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_World_Factbook_-_Grenada_8-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA_World_Factbook_-_Grenada-8">[8]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Foreign_relations">Foreign relations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Grenada&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Foreign relations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Further information: <a href="/wiki/Foreign_relations_of_Grenada" title="Foreign relations of Grenada">Foreign relations of Grenada</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Grenada is a full and participating member of both the <a href="/wiki/Caribbean_Community" title="Caribbean Community">Caribbean Community</a> (CARICOM) and the <a href="/wiki/Organisation_of_Eastern_Caribbean_States" title="Organisation of Eastern Caribbean States">Organisation of Eastern Caribbean States</a> (OECS).<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_World_Factbook_-_Grenada_8-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA_World_Factbook_-_Grenada-8">[8]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="The_Commonwealth">The Commonwealth</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Grenada&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: The Commonwealth">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <p>Grenada is, along with much of the Caribbean region, a member of the <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_of_Nations" title="Commonwealth of Nations">Commonwealth of Nations</a>. The organization, which primarily consists of former British colonies, focuses on fostering international relations between its members. </p> 
      <h4><span id="Organization_of_American_States_.28OAS.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Organization_of_American_States_(OAS)">Organization of American States (OAS)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Grenada&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Organization of American States (OAS)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <p>Grenada is one of the 35 states which has ratified the <a href="/wiki/Organization_of_American_States" title="Organization of American States">OAS</a> charter and is a member of the Organization.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">[64]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup> Grenada entered into the Inter-American system in 1975 according to the OAS's website.<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">[66]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h4><span id="Double_Taxation_Relief_.28CARICOM.29_Treaty"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Double_Taxation_Relief_(CARICOM)_Treaty">Double Taxation Relief (CARICOM) Treaty</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Grenada&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Double Taxation Relief (CARICOM) Treaty">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <p>On 6 July 1994 at <a href="/wiki/Lloyd_Erskine_Sandiford_Centre" title="Lloyd Erskine Sandiford Centre">Sherbourne Conference Centre</a> in St. Michael, <a href="/wiki/Barbados" title="Barbados">Barbados</a>, <a href="/wiki/George_Brizan" title="George Brizan">George Brizan</a> signed the Double Taxation Relief (CARICOM) Treaty on behalf of the Government of Grenada.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup> This treaty covered concepts such as taxes, residence, tax jurisdictions, capital gains, business profits, interest, dividends, royalties and other areas.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="FATCA">FATCA</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Grenada&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: FATCA">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <p>On 30 June 2014, Grenada signed a Model 1 agreement with the United States of America in relation to Foreign Account Tax Compliance Act (FATCA).<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Military">Military</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Grenada&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Military">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>Grenada has no standing military, leaving typical military functions to the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Grenada_Police_Force" title="Royal Grenada Police Force">Royal Grenada Police Force</a> (including a Special Service Unit) and the <a href="/wiki/Coast_Guard_of_Grenada" title="Coast Guard of Grenada">Coast Guard of Grenada</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_World_Factbook_-_Grenada_8-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA_World_Factbook_-_Grenada-8">[8]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In 2019, Grenada signed the UN treaty on the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_on_the_Prohibition_of_Nuclear_Weapons" title="Treaty on the Prohibition of Nuclear Weapons">Prohibition of Nuclear Weapons</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Administrative_divisions">Administrative divisions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Grenada&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Administrative divisions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Parishes_of_Grenada" title="Parishes of Grenada">Parishes of Grenada</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Grenada is divided into <a href="/wiki/Parishes_of_Grenada" title="Parishes of Grenada">six parishes</a>:<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_World_Factbook_-_Grenada_8-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA_World_Factbook_-_Grenada-8">[8]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Carriacou_and_Petite_Martinique" title="Carriacou and Petite Martinique">Carriacou and Petite Martinique</a> (<i>not pictured</i>) have the status of a dependency.<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_World_Factbook_-_Grenada_8-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA_World_Factbook_-_Grenada-8">[8]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="center">
       <div class="floatnone">
        <div class="noresize" style="height: 412px; width: 300px; ">
