      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Human_rights">Human rights</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Grenada&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Human rights">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/LGBT_rights_in_Grenada" title="LGBT rights in Grenada">LGBT rights in Grenada</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Male homosexuality is illegal in Grenada and punishable by prison time.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">[70]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Grenada&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Grenada" title="Economy of Grenada">Economy of Grenada</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Grenada has a small economy in which tourism is the major <a href="/wiki/Foreign_exchange_market" title="Foreign exchange market">foreign exchange</a> earner.<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_World_Factbook_-_Grenada_8-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA_World_Factbook_-_Grenada-8">[8]</a></sup> Major short-term concerns are the rising <a href="/wiki/Government_budget_deficit" class="mw-redirect" title="Government budget deficit">fiscal deficit</a> and the deterioration in the external account balance. Grenada shares a common <a href="/wiki/Central_bank" title="Central bank">central bank</a> and a common currency (the <a href="/wiki/East_Caribbean_dollar" class="mw-redirect" title="East Caribbean dollar">East Caribbean dollar</a>) with seven other members of the <a href="/wiki/Organisation_of_Eastern_Caribbean_States" title="Organisation of Eastern Caribbean States">Organisation of Eastern Caribbean States</a> (OECS).<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_World_Factbook_-_Grenada_8-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA_World_Factbook_-_Grenada-8">[8]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">[72]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Grenada has suffered from a heavy external debt problem, with government debt service payments running at about 25% of total revenues in 2017; Grenada was listed as ninth from bottom in a study of 126 developing countries.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">[73]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Agriculture_and_exports">Agriculture and exports</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Grenada&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Agriculture and exports">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Myris_fragr_Fr_080112-3294_ltn.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6c/Myris_fragr_Fr_080112-3294_ltn.jpg/220px-Myris_fragr_Fr_080112-3294_ltn.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="194" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6c/Myris_fragr_Fr_080112-3294_ltn.jpg/330px-Myris_fragr_Fr_080112-3294_ltn.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6c/Myris_fragr_Fr_080112-3294_ltn.jpg/440px-Myris_fragr_Fr_080112-3294_ltn.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1300" data-file-height="1144"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Myris_fragr_Fr_080112-3294_ltn.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Opened <a href="/wiki/Nutmeg" title="Nutmeg">nutmeg</a> fruit, showing the <a href="/wiki/Seed" title="Seed">seed</a> and the red <a href="/wiki/Aril" title="Aril">aril</a> used for <a href="/wiki/Mace_(spice)" class="mw-redirect" title="Mace (spice)">mace</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Grenada is an exporter of several different spices, most notably <a href="/wiki/Nutmeg" title="Nutmeg">nutmeg</a>, its top export and depicted on the national flag, and <a href="/wiki/Mace_(spice)" class="mw-redirect" title="Mace (spice)">mace</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">[74]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-britannica.com_9-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-britannica.com-9">[9]</a></sup> Other major exports include bananas, cocoa, fruit and vegetables, clothing, chocolate and fish.<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_World_Factbook_-_Grenada_8-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA_World_Factbook_-_Grenada-8">[8]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tourism">Tourism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Grenada&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Tourism">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>Tourism is the mainstay of Grenada's economy.<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_World_Factbook_-_Grenada_8-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA_World_Factbook_-_Grenada-8">[8]</a></sup> Conventional beach and water-sports tourism is largely focused in the southwest region around St George, the airport and the coastal strip. <a href="/wiki/Ecotourism" title="Ecotourism">Ecotourism</a> is growing in significance. Most small ecofriendly guesthouses are located in the <a href="/wiki/Saint_David_Parish,_Grenada" title="Saint David Parish, Grenada">Saint David</a> and <a href="/wiki/Saint_John_Parish,_Grenada" title="Saint John Parish, Grenada">Saint John</a> parishes. The tourism industry is increasing dramatically with the construction of a large cruise ship pier and esplanade. </p>
      <p> Tourism is concentrated in the southwest of the island, around St. George's, Grand Anse, Lance Aux Epines, and Point Salines. Grenada has many beaches around its coastline, including the 3&nbsp;km (1.9&nbsp;mi) long Grand Anse Beach in St George, often hailed as one of the best beaches in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup> Grenada's many waterfalls are also popular with tourists. The nearest to St. George's is the Annandale Waterfalls, but other notable ones like Mt. Carmel, Concord, Seven Sisters and Tufton Hall also being within easy reach.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">[76]</a></sup></p>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Grand_Anse_Beach_Grenada.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8c/Grand_Anse_Beach_Grenada.jpg/220px-Grand_Anse_Beach_Grenada.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="148" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8c/Grand_Anse_Beach_Grenada.jpg/330px-Grand_Anse_Beach_Grenada.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8c/Grand_Anse_Beach_Grenada.jpg/440px-Grand_Anse_Beach_Grenada.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2896" data-file-height="1944"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Grand_Anse_Beach_Grenada.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Grand Anse Beach, St. George's
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Several festivals also draw in tourists, such as Carriacou Maroon and String Band Music Festival in April,<sup id="cite_ref-auto_77-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto-77">[77]</a></sup> the Annual Budget Marine Spice Island Bill Fish Tournament,<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">[78]</a></sup> the Island Water World Sailing Week<sup id="cite_ref-grenadasailingweek.com_79-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-grenadasailingweek.com-79">[79]</a></sup> and the Grenada Sailing Festival Work Boat Regatta.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Grenada&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <p>Education in Grenada consists of kindergarten, pre-primary school, primary school, secondary school and tertiary education. The government has prioritised education, spending 10.3% of its budget to the sector in 2016, the third highest rate in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_World_Factbook_-_Grenada_8-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA_World_Factbook_-_Grenada-8">[8]</a></sup> Literacy rates are very high, with 98.6% of the population being able to read and write.<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_World_Factbook_-_Grenada_8-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA_World_Factbook_-_Grenada-8">[8]</a></sup> Schools include: </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Primary_Schools">Primary Schools</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Grenada&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Primary Schools">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

       <li><a href="/wiki/Grenada_Boys%27_Secondary_School" title="Grenada Boys' Secondary School">Grenada Boys' Secondary School</a>, established in 1885</li>
      </ul> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tertiary_education">Tertiary education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Grenada&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Tertiary education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <ul>
       <li>New Life Organisation (NEWLO)</li> 
       <li>T.A. Marryshow Community College</li> 
       <li>UWI Open Campus in Grenada</li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/St._George%27s_University" title="St. George's University">St. George's University</a>, one of the Organisation of American States (OAS) Consortium of Universities<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">[80]</a></sup></li>
      </ul> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Transport">Transport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Grenada&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Transport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <p><a href="/wiki/Maurice_Bishop_International_Airport" title="Maurice Bishop International Airport">Maurice Bishop International Airport</a> is the country's main airport,<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_World_Factbook_-_Grenada_8-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA_World_Factbook_-_Grenada-8">[8]</a></sup> connecting the country with other Caribbean islands, the United States, Canada, and Europe. There is also an airport on Carriacou.<sup id="cite_ref-Encyclopedia_Britannica_-_Grenada_19-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Encyclopedia_Britannica_-_Grenada-19">[19]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Grenada&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Demographics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_Grenada" title="Demographics of Grenada">Demographics of Grenada</a>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Further information: <a href="/wiki/Afro-Grenadians" title="Afro-Grenadians">Afro-Grenadians</a>, <a href="/wiki/Indo-Grenadians" title="Indo-Grenadians">Indo-Grenadians</a>, and <a href="/wiki/List_of_cities_in_Grenada" title="List of cities in Grenada">List of cities in Grenada</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Carriacou_Scene.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f0/Carriacou_Scene.jpg/220px-Carriacou_Scene.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f0/Carriacou_Scene.jpg/330px-Carriacou_Scene.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f0/Carriacou_Scene.jpg/440px-Carriacou_Scene.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2288" data-file-height="1712"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Carriacou_Scene.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>A view of <a href="/wiki/Carriacou" title="Carriacou">Carriacou</a>, with other Grenadine islands visible in the distance
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>A majority of Grenadians (82%<sup id="cite_ref-cia.gov_2-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cia.gov-2">[2]</a></sup>) are descendants of the <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_slave_trade" title="Atlantic slave trade">enslaved Africans</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_World_Factbook_-_Grenada_8-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA_World_Factbook_-_Grenada-8">[8]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Encyclopedia_Britannica_-_Grenada_19-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Encyclopedia_Britannica_-_Grenada-19">[19]</a></sup> Few of the indigenous Carib and Arawak population survived the French purge at <a href="/wiki/Sauteurs" title="Sauteurs">Sauteurs</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> A small percentage of descendants of indentured workers from <a href="/wiki/India" title="India">India</a> were brought to Grenada between 1857 and 1885, predominantly from the states of <a href="/wiki/Bihar" title="Bihar">Bihar</a> and <a href="/wiki/Uttar_Pradesh" title="Uttar Pradesh">Uttar Pradesh</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Today, Grenadians of Indian descent constitute 2.2% of the population.<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_World_Factbook_-_Grenada_8-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA_World_Factbook_-_Grenada-8">[8]</a></sup> There is also a small community of French and English descendants.<sup id="cite_ref-Encyclopedia_Britannica_-_Grenada_19-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Encyclopedia_Britannica_-_Grenada-19">[19]</a></sup> The rest of the population is of mixed descent (13%).<sup id="cite_ref-cia.gov_2-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cia.gov-2">[2]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Grenada, like many of the Caribbean islands, is subject to a large amount of out-migration, with a large number of young people seeking more prospects abroad. Popular migration points for Grenadians include more prosperous islands in the Caribbean (such as <a href="/wiki/Barbados" title="Barbados">Barbados</a>), North American Cities (such as New York City, Toronto and <a href="/wiki/Montreal" title="Montreal">Montreal</a>), the United Kingdom (in particular, London and <a href="/wiki/Yorkshire" title="Yorkshire">Yorkshire</a>; see <a href="/wiki/Grenadian_British" class="mw-redirect" title="Grenadian British">Grenadians in the UK</a>) and Australia.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Grenada&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Religion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Languages">Languages</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Grenada&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Languages">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>English is the country's official language<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_World_Factbook_-_Grenada_8-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA_World_Factbook_-_Grenada-8">[8]</a></sup> but the main spoken language is either of two <a href="/wiki/Creole_language" title="Creole language">creole languages</a> (<a href="/wiki/Grenadian_Creole_English" title="Grenadian Creole English">Grenadian Creole English</a> and, less frequently, <a href="/wiki/Grenadian_Creole_French" title="Grenadian Creole French">Grenadian Creole French</a>) (sometimes called 'patois') which reflects the African, European, and native heritage of the nation. The creoles contain elements from a variety of African languages, French and English. <a href="/wiki/Grenadian_Creole_French" title="Grenadian Creole French">Grenadian Creole French</a> is mainly spoken in smaller rural areas.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p>
      <p>Some <a href="/wiki/Hindi" title="Hindi">Hindi</a>/<a href="/wiki/Bhojpuri" class="mw-redirect" title="Bhojpuri">Bhojpuri</a> terms are still spoken amongst the Indo-Grenadian community descendants.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p>
      <p>The indigenous languages were <a href="/wiki/I%C3%B1eri_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Iñeri language">Iñeri</a> and <a href="/wiki/Karina_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Karina language">Karina</a> (Carib).<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Grenada&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_Grenada" title="Culture of Grenada">Culture of Grenada</a> and <a href="/wiki/Music_of_Grenada" title="Music of Grenada">Music of Grenada</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:GrenadaCarnival1965FeatheredHeaddresses.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/GrenadaCarnival1965FeatheredHeaddresses.jpg/220px-GrenadaCarnival1965FeatheredHeaddresses.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="210" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/GrenadaCarnival1965FeatheredHeaddresses.jpg/330px-GrenadaCarnival1965FeatheredHeaddresses.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/GrenadaCarnival1965FeatheredHeaddresses.jpg/440px-GrenadaCarnival1965FeatheredHeaddresses.jpg 2x" data-file-width="903" data-file-height="863"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:GrenadaCarnival1965FeatheredHeaddresses.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>A carnival in 1965
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Island culture is heavily influenced by the <a href="/wiki/Ethnic_groups_of_Africa" class="mw-redirect" title="Ethnic groups of Africa">African</a> roots of most of the Grenadians, coupled with the country's long experience of colonial rule under the British. Although French influence on Grenadian culture is much less visible than on some other <a href="/wiki/Caribbean_islands" class="mw-redirect" title="Caribbean islands">Caribbean islands</a>, surnames and place names in French remain, and the everyday language is laced with French words and the local Creole, or Patois.<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_World_Factbook_-_Grenada_8-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA_World_Factbook_-_Grenada-8">[8]</a></sup> Stronger French influence is found in the well seasoned <a href="/wiki/Spice" title="Spice">spicy food</a> and styles of cooking similar to those found in <a href="/wiki/New_Orleans" title="New Orleans">New Orleans</a>, and some French architecture has survived from the 1700s.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Indian and <a href="/wiki/Island_Caribs" class="mw-redirect" title="Island Caribs">Carib Amerindian</a> influence is also seen, especially in the island's cuisine. </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Oil_down" title="Oil down">Oil down</a>, a stew, is considered to be the national dish.<sup id="cite_ref-Gov.gd_82-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gov.gd-82">[82]</a></sup> The name refers to a dish cooked in coconut milk until all the milk is absorbed, leaving a bit of coconut oil in the bottom of the pot. Early recipes call for a mixture of salted pigtail, pig's feet (trotters), salt beef and chicken, dumplings made from flour, and provision like breadfruit, green banana, yam and potatoes. <a href="/wiki/Callaloo" title="Callaloo">Callaloo</a> leaves are sometimes used to retain the steam and add extra flavour.<sup id="cite_ref-Gov.gd_82-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gov.gd-82">[82]</a></sup> </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Soca_music" title="Soca music">Soca</a>, <a href="/wiki/Calypso_music" title="Calypso music">calypso</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Reggae" title="Reggae">reggae</a> are popular music genres and are played at Grenada's annual <a href="/wiki/Carnival" title="Carnival">Carnival</a>. Over the years <a href="/wiki/Rap" class="mw-redirect" title="Rap">rap</a> music became popular amongst Grenadian youths, and there have been numerous young rappers emerging in the island's underground rap scene.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> <a href="/wiki/Zouk_(musical_movement)" class="mw-redirect" title="Zouk (musical movement)">Zouk</a> is also being slowly introduced onto the island.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p>
      <p>An important aspect of the Grenadian culture is the tradition of <a href="/wiki/Storytelling" title="Storytelling">story telling</a>, with <a href="/wiki/Folklore" title="Folklore">folk tales</a> bearing both African and French influences.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> The character, <i><a href="/wiki/Anansi" title="Anansi">Anancy</a></i>, a spider who is a <a href="/wiki/Trickster" title="Trickster">trickster</a>, originated in West Africa and is prevalent on other islands as well. French influence can be seen in <i><a href="/wiki/La_Diablesse" title="La Diablesse">La Diablesse</a></i>, a well-dressed she-<a href="/wiki/Devil" title="Devil">devil</a>, and <i><a href="/wiki/Loogaroo" class="mw-redirect" title="Loogaroo">Loogaroo</a></i> (from "loup-garou"), a <a href="/wiki/Werewolf" title="Werewolf">werewolf</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Sports">Sports</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Grenada&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: Sports">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Olympics">Olympics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Grenada&amp;action=edit&amp;section=40" title="Edit section: Olympics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Grenada_at_the_Olympics" title="Grenada at the Olympics">Grenada at the Olympics</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:162px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Kirani_James_Daegu_2011.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Kirani_James_Daegu_2011.jpg/160px-Kirani_James_Daegu_2011.jpg" decoding="async" width="160" height="240" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Kirani_James_Daegu_2011.jpg/240px-Kirani_James_Daegu_2011.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Kirani_James_Daegu_2011.jpg/320px-Kirani_James_Daegu_2011.jpg 2x" data-file-width="426" data-file-height="640"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Kirani_James_Daegu_2011.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Kirani James, noted Grenadian sprinter
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Grenada has competed in every Summer Olympics since the <a href="/wiki/1984_Summer_Olympics" title="1984 Summer Olympics">1984 Summer Olympics</a> in Los Angeles.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> <a href="/wiki/Kirani_James" title="Kirani James">Kirani James</a> won the first Olympic <a href="/wiki/Gold_medal" title="Gold medal">gold medal</a> for Grenada in the <a href="/wiki/Athletics_at_the_2012_Summer_Olympics_%E2%80%93_Men%27s_400_metres" title="Athletics at the 2012 Summer Olympics – Men's 400 metres">men's 400 meters</a> in <a href="/wiki/2012_Summer_Olympics" title="2012 Summer Olympics">2012</a> in London and silver in <a href="/wiki/2016_Summer_Olympics" title="2016 Summer Olympics">2016</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cricket">Cricket</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Grenada&amp;action=edit&amp;section=41" title="Edit section: Cricket">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/Cricket_in_the_West_Indies" title="Cricket in the West Indies">Cricket in the West Indies</a> and <a href="/wiki/Windward_Islands_cricket_team" title="Windward Islands cricket team">Windward Islands cricket team</a>
      </div> 
      <p>As with other islands from the Caribbean, <a href="/wiki/Cricket" title="Cricket">cricket</a> is the national and most popular sport and is an intrinsic part of Grenadian culture. The <a href="/wiki/Grenada_national_cricket_team" title="Grenada national cricket team">Grenada national cricket team</a> forms a part of the <a href="/wiki/Windward_Islands_cricket_team" title="Windward Islands cricket team">Windward Islands cricket team</a> in regional domestic cricket, however it plays as a separate entity in minor regional matches,<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">[83]</a></sup> as well as having previously played <a href="/wiki/Twenty20" title="Twenty20">Twenty20</a> cricket in the <a href="/wiki/Stanford_20/20" title="Stanford 20/20">Stanford 20/20</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">[84]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Grenada_National_Cricket_Stadium" class="mw-redirect" title="Grenada National Cricket Stadium">Grenada National Cricket Stadium</a> in <a href="/wiki/St._George%27s,_Grenada" title="St. George's, Grenada">St. George's</a> hosts domestic and international cricket matches. <a href="/wiki/Devon_Smith" title="Devon Smith">Devon Smith</a>, West Indies record holder to win the <a href="/wiki/List-A_cricket" class="mw-redirect" title="List-A cricket">List-A</a> West Indian <a href="/wiki/WICB_Cup" class="mw-redirect" title="WICB Cup">domestic competition</a> for the second time, was born in the small town of <a href="/wiki/Hermitage_(Carriacou)" title="Hermitage (Carriacou)">Hermitage</a>. </p>
      <p>In April 2007 Grenada jointly hosted (along with several other Caribbean nations) the <a href="/wiki/2007_Cricket_World_Cup" title="2007 Cricket World Cup">2007 Cricket World Cup</a>. The Island's Prime Minister was the <a href="/wiki/CARICOM" class="mw-redirect" title="CARICOM">CARICOM</a> representative on cricket and was instrumental in having the World Cup games brought to the region. After Hurricane Ivan, the government of the <a href="/wiki/People%27s_Republic_of_China" class="mw-redirect" title="People's Republic of China">People's Republic of China</a> (PRC) paid for the new $40&nbsp;million <a href="/wiki/Queen%27s_Park,_Grenada" class="mw-redirect" title="Queen's Park, Grenada">national stadium</a> and provided the aid of over 300 labourers to build and repair it.<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">[85]</a></sup> During the opening ceremony, the anthem of the <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_China" class="mw-redirect" title="Republic of China">Republic of China</a> (ROC, <a href="/wiki/Taiwan" title="Taiwan">Taiwan</a>) was accidentally played instead of the PRC's anthem, leading to the firing of top officials.<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">[86]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">[87]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notable_people">Notable people</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Grenada&amp;action=edit&amp;section=42" title="Edit section: Notable people">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <ul>
       <li><a href="/wiki/Sydney_Gun-Munro" title="Sydney Gun-Munro">Sydney Gun-Munro</a>, First Governor General of <a href="/wiki/Saint_Vincent_and_the_Grenadines" title="Saint Vincent and the Grenadines">Saint Vincent and the Grenadines</a></li>
      </ul>
